## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of time t and current concentration A, which is the fundamental problem of chemical kinetics rate law determination. The rate typically depends on concentration through power-law or more complex functional forms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate expression)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (transition between first and zero order)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (sum of first and second order pathways)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with constant product)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product catalyzes its own formation)
- Time-dependent decay with order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-modulated rate)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2 (substrate inhibition)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (empirical fractional order with baseline)
- Consecutive reaction intermediate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (intermediate species in sequential mechanism)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited or heterogeneous kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence of rate on concentration → first-order kinetics, dA_dt = c*A
- Rate proportional to concentration squared → second-order kinetics or bimolecular mechanism
- Rate that saturates at high concentration → enzyme-like or surface-limited kinetics with rational form A/(1+c*A)
- Parabolic concentration dependence (rate peaks then decreases) → autocatalytic or substrate-inhibited mechanism A*(c1-A)
- Rate with explicit time dependence beyond what A captures → non-autonomous system, photolysis, or externally driven process
- Log-linear relationship between rate and concentration → power-law kinetics with fractional order
- Rate approaching a constant at high A → zero-order regime, saturation kinetics
- Negative rate values (consumption) with sign change → reversible reaction near equilibrium
- Rate depending on both A and t multiplicatively → heterogeneous or diffusion-controlled kinetics where geometry evolves with time

1. A linear term in A: `-0.25667*A`

3. `sin(log(A+1))`: a sine of logarithm term

The GT has three fundamentally different basis functions: `A`, `A*exp(αt)`, and `sin(log(A+1))`.

Let me now check each candidate. The critical question is whether any candidate can produce the `sin(log(A+1))` term, since this is a very specific nonlinear function.

**Key observation:** `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be represented by polynomials in A, rational functions of A, power functions `A^c`, `log(A)`, `exp(A)`, or simple combinations thereof. This is because `sin(log(A+1))` is an oscillatory function (for large A) that no polynomial, rational, exponential, or power function can replicate exactly.

Let me scan through candidates looking for any that contain `sin(log(...))` or equivalent:

- **Candidate 44:** Contains `sin(c7*log(c8*t + 1) + c9)` — this is sin of log in **t**, not in A. Cannot match.

None of the candidates contain `sin(log(A + c))` or any equivalent oscillatory function of A.

Let me verify: Could any candidate's `A^c` term approximate `sin(log(A+1))`? No — `A^c` is a monotonic power function, while `sin(log(A+1))` oscillates. These are fundamentally different basis functions and cannot be equivalent.

Could `log(c*exp(A*c) + 1)` (Candidates 27, 43) produce `sin(log(A+1))`? No — softplus-like functions are monotonic, not oscillatory.

Could `exp(A^2*c)` terms help? No — exponentials of polynomials are monotonic in A for fixed sign.

Could `(A+1)^c` (Candidates 3, 7, 49) help? `(A+1)^c` for complex c could theoretically produce oscillatory behavior, but in symbolic regression we restrict to real constants. For real c, `(A+1)^c` is monotonic and cannot match `sin(log(A+1))`.

Let me verify each candidate systematically:

Candidates 1-50: None contain `sin(log(A+...))` or any equivalent construction. The `sin` function appears only in Candidate 44 (with argument involving t, not A). The `cos` function appears in Candidates 45, 47 (with argument involving t, not A).
